< Text>
Notice! Fraud activity in this gas station!!

I wanna report a fraud activity from 76 gas station at 8755 W 3rd street, Los Angeles, CA, 90048

The owner of this 76 gas station intentionally confuse the term of "full service" . They let you to fuel the tank by yourself just like what we did in 99.99% of the gas stations in CA, but quietly surcharge you $0.5 / gallon without mentioning a single word about it.

I noticed the price difference after I fueled the tank myself. Then, I came and found them. They then explained to me that "full service" means they fuel the tank for me. In my case, although I fueled the tank myself, they still charge me the price without saying a single word, but quietly put the price in the gas price.

The price they overcharged me was pretty small, a few dollars. But the feeling of being cheated makes me extremely angry. I also noticed some other cars parked in those "full service" areas. I believe a lot of people were also cheated in the same way.

It is a shame of 76 gas. These dishonest people need to be punished.< /Text>

<time>1584328011701< /time>< Review>
My Thai @ Capitola Beach is my favorite local Thai restaurant. I actually have to drive further out because I prefer My Thai to my local.

The owner, Pinky and her relative, Sun, are always cheerful and are eager to please. My Thai has the ‚Äústandard dishes that is everybody‚Äôs favorite.‚Äù The fresh flavored dishes are complimented in an artful  presentation and can range to whatever degree of hotness that you like, but don‚Äôt forget to tell them. There are as many vegetarian options as there are meat. They really mean to please and will adjust dishes according to your preference.

I don‚Äôt drink alcoholic beverages, so I can‚Äôt comment on that. My go to drink is the Iced Thai  Tea.

I love the ‚ÄúBasil Dish‚Äù and have ordered that both as a vegetarian dish and as a dish with meat. Another fav is the ‚ÄúSweet Potato Thai Style Tampura‚Äù and both the fried and the fresh ‚ÄúSpring Rolls.‚Äù Snd don‚Äôt forget dessert. If you select the ‚ÄúFried Banana‚Äù, I recommend that you do it with Ice Cream!  Dishes are reasonably priced.

I love the country home feeling ambiance, and call ahead to reserve the table window. It‚Äôs a great place to bring a friend or small party on a Friyay night before burning calories dancing next door.

Check them out on your next visit to Capitola.

Bon Appetit!  And in case you are wondering, there is no outside seating. The parking is Pay by the Space street parking until 8pm.
And oh!  Take Out options!<//Review>

<user>109555225237723138139</user>< Name>
Luke Keppler< /Name>
< Date>
1324867674537</Date>
<Rating>1< /Rating><text>Small portions and oily, fried tofu.

I came here for Christmas dinner, looking to load up on papaya salad, and maybe a little curry.  When we entered the restaurant, the first thing we noticed was the fantastic view.  This is a beautiful place to eat.

The waitress finally arrived, I politely asked how big a papaya salad is because I wanted to know whether to order 1 or 2-3.  She said it would be enough for one person and probably be able to give someone else a bit, too.  So, I ordered one.  She lied.  The papaya salad is about one handful of ingredients, spread out on a plate of juice.  The flavor and presentation of the papaya salad were great, but it wasn't even close to a meal, let alone a side-salad.  And the salad was the price of a full-sized meal.  WAAAY too expensive!

I asked whether the Hot Pepper w/ Tofu and Vegetables was sweet.  The waitress said "no, no no!".  I went ahead with one of those.  It was incredibly salty.  Inedible, really.  It tasted like seawater.  On top of that, it was very sweet, like sweet chili sauce, something I didn't want due to my diet.  And on top of that, it was served with fried tofu.  Now I've been to good Thai restaurants that are offended when I ask them not to fry the tofu, and here's one, stuck in last century, still frying the living daylights out of its tofu.  So fried, it doesn't absorb the flavor of the sauce because it is already saturated in oil!

Before that order arrived, I also ordered a Red Curry with Vegetables and Tofu.  Obviously, the tofu was also deep fried.  Moreover, the vegetables in the curry were limp and flavorless.  Not fresh, not lightly simmered.  They were either days-old veggies, or they'd stewed the living daylights out of them until they were down to mush.

After noticing the oil, I wanted to press some of the oil out of my veggies.  Unfortunately I couldn't even do that because the plate you get when you order a la cart is tiny and there was no room left after pushing aside the greasy sauce and soggy vegetables.  There are also no paper napkins as an alternative to the single linen napkin that I'd already spit a bunch of oily phlegm into while clearing my throat.

If you want Chinese food style Thai food, you found the place.  You'll get the communication barrier and the smell of burning oil, the sound of woks clanking around in the kitchen as they fry the heck out of everything.  If, however, you want an elegant Thai dinner in real quantities where they actually care about your long-term health, go elsewhere.<//text>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>
<resp>None</resp>< gmapID>

Here are some tips for a successful consumership at this location.
1) Emphasize the descriptive word HOT if you are ordering a hot cup of coffee.  If you don't, better have a microwave where you are going.
2) If you request sugar of any type, ask if they can stir it!
3) Avoid the drive-thru at all costs if you have a headache.   Someone there really likes their tunes loud, even outside.
4) Be someone not caring if the barista likes their job.

Thank you!</text>

< Text>
One Way is a nifty new "old-fashioned burger joint". The food is comparable to The Habit and A&W as far as taste, prices but a lot of their servings are a bit bigger. They have ice cream, sundaes, shakes and a. Couple other yummy desserts that are priced just right. The people there are nice, helpful and polite. The only drawback is it's right across the street from the oval park. The food is worth it tho.< /Text>

<text>Make sure to read the whole review!üòÅ
üí¢Let's start with location- this burger joint is located in the downtown area of visalia, right across from the oval park. The park is know to be home to some of visalias unsavory people, but they do not pan Handel restaurant goers and do not bother. Make sure to lock your car before going in and eating but that's just a given for any restaurant.
üí¢Exterior- The owners did a wonderful job giving this joint a new fresh coat of paint, and putting up their lively signs out front! It doesn't look run down or unclean. The inside is also very clean as well.
üí¢Customer service- This is hard to gage because of not having any seating open due to covid. However, the customer service we received when ordering and paying was wonderful. They were kind and very patient with me, becuase I have a hard time making fast decisions. The gentleman taking my order was polite and cared about my special requests for my burger.
üí¢FINALLY the food! - So we ordered, a cheese burger combo, al carte cheese burger, a chicken tenders combo, and a ice cream cone. All that food for about 25$ thats including tax!! Thats a steal for eating take out these days folks, and all that food could have easily fed 3 people and a child. Everything is made fresh to order, the fries are not sitting out in a warmer and they are perfectly crisp but not over done. The burgers though! Fresh made with Harris rach Patty'sü§§ mmm you can't do any better. These burgers were on par, and better than best burger! The veggies used in the burger were also very fresh and crisp.
The chicken tenders, I have been told are there most popular item on the menu, and for a good reason. They are perfectly crispy, not fatty and not all batter, great for the priceüòã
üí¢Over view üí¢
We will eat here again of course. Great food choice because the other restaurants around the oval are of different cuisine and this is great American faire food. I personally would love to see the park cleaned up and patrolled so we can have kids play on the playground and families walking around, so we can enjoy take out meals outside on the picnic benches because they are so close.
üí¢Suggestion for ownersüí¢
Sign up with uber eats or grubhub, or any delivery service!! You would be a hit on one of those apps considering not everyone feels safe coming to that part of town. (Unfortunately).< /text></record></dataset><record>

<name>Dragon Garcia< /name><time>1582047980714<//time>< Rating>
5<//Rating>
< text>
I like coming Monday and Tuesday nights for their open mics. The environment is very inviting and full of culture with so many poets, musicians, and artists of all realms. Last night, this lovely singer-songwriter's keyboard malfunctioned, initially impeding her ability to perform. She was the last act of the night, the clock was ticking, the MC had to start getting everyone out by 11. However, when she asked if she should just pack her keyboard and skip her turn, applause and cheers of encouragement erupted and filled the room. Moments into this girl singing acapella, one by one everyone in the crowd began to snap along to the bluesy beat of her song. Snaps turned into claps, one guy started knocking on a table and playing with the rhythm, another pulled a maraca out of his bag, and voices in the background could be heard vocalizing and giving her the accompaniment she had been stressing about earlier. It was a beautiful, unreal experience. So yeah, if you're looking for a cool coffee shop with good food and drinks (and a few vegan options, I might add), then I highly recommend you go support your local business and get a taste of their vibe, meanwhile checking out a super supportive artistic community.< /text>

< Review>
I write for a music and coffee blog called Crooners In Coffeeshops, in which I interview local musicians at local coffeeshops. My writeup reflects the positive experience that I encountered at Back To The Grind on our interview date.

Smack dab in between numerous schools, hotels, the courthouse, and the convention center, Back to Grind has been serving the Riverside community for twenty long and happy years. Its quirky and artistic with a hint of vintage exterior initially draws you in, but it‚Äôs the shop‚Äôs interior that makes you want to stay there all day curled up with a book, playing board games, or simply to just get some work done in a fun environment.  Brick walls, weathered hardwood floors, and a high, ornate ceiling adds to the old-timey feel of the place, while modern music and artwork of many variations (installations, sculptures, paintings, knick knacks, etc.) are on display on the walls, tables, pillars, and giant library-esque bookshelf.

But don‚Äôt judge a book by it‚Äôs cover with this place, because they know how to throw a party! With regular music showcases, game tournaments, open mic nights, poetry readings, and even weddings, Back to the Grind is a perfect location to host an array of different types of events. With plenty of space to move around in and an abundance of seating inside, outside, and upstairs in their loft area, what more could you ask for? Oh, right, dranks! With a decent selection of classic coffee and tea options along with your choice of a healthy (or decadent) bite to eat, you‚Äôre pretty much set for however amount of time you are looking to spend there. In fact, after 12pm you can transition into beer o‚Äô clock, which unfortunately is a rare sight to see these days. Make sure that you bring enough cash to try everything because the shop is cash only, but if you forget, there‚Äôs an ATM machine for use conveniently inside so there is no excuse for you to not get yourself a little somethin‚Äô somethin.‚Äô<//Review>

< text>
My Favourite Coffee Place.

For me Back to the Grind is a special place. Reasonable prices, plenty of stuff to buy with your coffee (including ice cream and vegan offerings), Plenty going on, yet really chill, I could go on and on. Unlike certain corporate competitors, Back to the Grind has a unique and welcoming atmosphere; it is absolutely covered in art, and staff are always friendly and timely. There are also events like the open mike night, or the occasional gathering for chess. It is the perfect place to relax and read with your drink of choice, or meet up with friends. Bring your own mug! You'll thank me later.</text>

CASH ONLY!! That said, there is an atm inside and this place is walking distance from the Mission Inn (Highly recommend you stay here). This coffee shop is large and great for groups, has a large menu and does events!

A group of us came on a Thursday morning and they only had 1 barista working so the wait was quite long. They have everything from pastries, oatmeal, fruit smoothies, & bagels. Prices are typical of a coffee shop. I paid $4.45 for a decaf almond milk latte (small sized).

I appreciated that they grind the espresso beans when you order a drink which adds to the depth of flavor. I didn't attend the events but I did see they have a lot of local features like an art walk on the first Thursday and they have free wifi!< /text>

<text>Back to the Grind is Riverside's alternative coffee house.

In business for over a decade, I would study here after school. The staff is friendly, knowledgeable and passionate about their coffee. I enjoy their cappuccinos and various teas.

They offer free wi-fi, have events (open mic nights, art exhibits, etc) all the time, and you're bound to see someone interesting looking when you come in.

They probably have the best ceiling any coffee house has, and their bookshelves always have something interesting to pick out.

Note: They are a cash only place, so be aware of it. ATM is available for you.</text><Pics>None< /Pics><response>None<//response>< GmapID>
